        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Li-ion battery technol. has become very important in recent years as these batteries show great promise as power sources that can lead us to the elec. vehicle (EV) revolution.  The development of new materials for Li-ion batteries is the focus of research in prominent groups in the field of materials science throughout the world.  Li-ion batteries can be considered to be the most impressive success story of modern electrochem. in the last two decades.  They power most of today's portable devices, and seem to overcome the psychol. barriers against the use of such high energy d. devices on a larger scale for more demanding applications, such as EV.  Since this field is advancing rapidly and attracting an increasing no. of researchers, it is important to provide current and timely updates of this constantly changing technol.  In this review, we describe the key aspects of Li-ion batteries: the basic science behind their operation, the most relevant components, anodes, cathodes, electrolyte solns., as well as important future directions for R&amp;D of advanced Li-ion batteries for demanding use, such as EV and load-leveling applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref4" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1039/c2ee02781j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Palomares, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Serras, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Villaluenga, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hueso, K.                         cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-ion batteries, recent advances and present challenges to become low cost energy storage systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Palomares, Veronica; Serras, Paula; Villaluenga, Irune; Hueso, Karina B.; Carretero-Gonzalez, Javier; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref5" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.cossms.2012.04.002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ellis, B.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Owing to almost unmatched volumetric energy d., Li-ion batteries have dominated the portable electronics industry and solid state electrochem. literature for the past 20 years.  Not only will that continue, but they are also now powering plug-in hybrid elec. vehicles and elec. vehicles.  In light of possible concerns over rising lithium costs in the future, Na and Na-ion batteries have re-emerged as candidates for medium and large-scale stationary energy storage, esp. as a result of heightened interest in renewable energy sources that provide intermittent power which needs to be load-levelled.  The sodium-ion battery field presents many solid state materials design challenges, and rising to that call in the past couple of years, several reports of new sodium-ion technologies and electrode materials have surfaced.  These range from high-temp. air electrodes to new layered oxides, polyanion-based materials, carbons and other insertion materials for sodium-ion batteries, many of which hold promise for future sodium-based energy storage applications.  In this article, the challenges of current high-temp. sodium technologies including Na-S and Na-NiCl2 and new molten sodium technol., Na-O2 are summarized.  Recent advancements in pos. and neg. electrode materials suitable for Na-ion and hybrid Na/Li-ion cells are reviewed, along with the prospects for future developments.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref6" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201200691"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Slater, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Si-based Li-ion battery anodes have recently received great attention, as they offer specific capacity an order of magnitude beyond that of conventional graphite.  The applications of this transformative technol. require synthesis routes capable of producing safe and easy-to-handle anode particles with low vol. changes and stable performance during battery operation.  Herein, we report a large-scale hierarchical bottom-up assembly route for the formation of Si on the nanoscale-contg. rigid and robust spheres with irregular channels for rapid access of Li ions into the particle bulk.  Large Si vol. changes on Li insertion and extn. are accommodated by the particle's internal porosity.  Reversible capacities over five times higher than that of the state-of-the-art anodes and stable performance are attained.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrode materials for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries: potential alternatives to current lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Sung-Wook; Seo, Dong-Hwa; Ma, Xiaohua; Ceder, Gerbrand; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium (Li)-ion batteries (LIB) have governed the current worldwide rechargeable battery market due to their outstanding energy and power capability.  In particular, the LIB's role in enabling elec. vehicles (EVs) has been highlighted to replace the current oil-driven vehicles in order to reduce the usage of oil resources and generation of CO2 gases.  Unlike Li, sodium is one of the more abundant elements on Earth and exhibits similar chem. properties to Li, indicating that Na chem. could be applied to a similar battery system.  In the 1970s-80s, both Na-ion and Li-ion electrodes were investigated, but the higher energy d. of Li-ion cells made them more applicable to small, portable electronic devices, and research efforts for rechargeable batteries have been mainly concd. on LIB since then.  Recently, research interest in Na-ion batteries (NIB) has been resurrected, driven by new applications with requirements different from those in portable electronics, and to address the concern on Li abundance.  In this article, both neg. and pos. electrode materials in NIB are briefly reviewed.  While the voltage is generally lower and the vol. change upon Na removal or insertion is larger for Na-intercalation electrodes, compared to their Li equiv., the power capability can vary depending on the crystal structures.  It is concluded that cost-effective NIB can partially replace LIB, but requires further investigation and improvement.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref14" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1039/C3NR05022J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zeng, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Y.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">6</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">693</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">698</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phosphorus-carbon nanocomposite anodes for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ramireddy, Thrinathreddy; Xing, Tan; Rahman, Md Mokhlesur; Chen, Ying; Dutercq, Quentin; Gunzelmann, Daniel; Glushenkov, Alexey M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">With the expected theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1, P is considered to be the highest capacity anode material for Na-ion batteries and one of the most attractive anode materials for Li-ion systems.  This work presents a comprehensive study of P-C nanocomposite anodes for both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  The composite electrodes are able to display high initial capacities of ∼1700 and 1300 mA h g-1 in Li and Na half-cells, resp., when the cells are tested within a larger potential windows of 2.0-0.01 V vs. Li/Li+ and Na/Na+.  The level of demonstrated capacity is underpinned by the storage mechanism, based on the transformation of P to Li3P phase for Li cells and an incomplete transformation to Na3P phase for Na cells.  The capacity deteriorates upon cycling, which is shown to originate from disintegration of electrodes and their delamination from current collectors by post-cycling ex situ electron microscopy.  Stable cyclic performance at the level of ∼700 and ∼350-400 mA h g-1 can be achieved if the potential windows are restricted to 2.0-0.67 V vs. Li/Li+ for Li and 2-0.33 vs. Na/Na+ for Na half-cells.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Crystalline red phosphorus incorporated with porous carbon nanofibers as flexible electrode for high performance lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Weihan; Yang, Zhenzhong; Jiang, Yu; Yu, Zirui; Gu, Lin; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Here we demonstrated porous carbon nanofibers encapsulated with cryst. red P (P-PCNFs) as free-standing anodes for LIBs with high specific capacity and excellent electrochem. cycling.  The porous carbon nanofibers were fabricated by electrospinning of polyacrylonitrile/poly(Me methacrylate) (PAN/PMMA), followed by thermal carbonization process.  The P-PCNFs delivered an excellent cyclability (∼2030 mAh g-1 at 0.1C rate after 100 cycles) and outstanding rate capability (380 mAh g-1 at 11C for 10 cycles), where those capacity values were calcd. based on the red P percentage.  Even at a rate of 1C, this composite could deliver a superior capacity of 1042 mAh g-1 based on the content of red P after 100 cycles.  The pores of porous carbon nanofibers could effectively accommodate the vol. change of cryst. red P during cycling.  Furthermore, the carbon nanofibers matrix not only enables fast access of ions but also grants the electrode with good cond. and high mech. flexibility.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref17" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1021/nl501617j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, H.-W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yao, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, Y.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">14</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">4573</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">4580</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

    </div><div class="casAbstract">The d.c. resistance of amorphous red P was measured at ≤90 kbar.  A transition to orthorhombic black P occurred at 70 kbar.  At fixed pressure, a time dependent variation of resistance occurred due to relaxation of the glass structure.  Temp. dependence of the resistance at const. pressure suggests that the variable-range hopping becomes the dominant conduction mechanism as pressure is increased; an increase in the no. of defect sites is responsible for the decrease in resistance.  A comparison is made with other materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref19" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1002/adma.200602592"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, C.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A phosphorene-graphene hybrid material as a high-capacity anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Jie; Lee, Hyun-Wook; Pasta, Mauro; Yuan, Hongtao; Zheng, Guangyuan; Sun, Yongming; Li, Yuzhang; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Nanotechnology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">980-985</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NNAABX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1748-3387</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have recently attracted significant attention as an alternative to Li-ion batteries because Na sources do not present the geopolitical issues that Li sources might.  Although recent reports on cathode materials for Na-ion batteries demonstrated performances comparable to their Li-ion counterparts, the major scientific challenge for a competitive Na-ion battery technol. is to develop viable anode materials.  A hybrid material made out of a few phosphorene layers sandwiched between graphene layers shows a specific capacity of 2 440 mA h g-1 (calcd. using the mass of P only) at a c.d. of 0.05 A g-1 and an 83% capacity retention after 100 cycles while operating between 0 and 1.5 V.  Using in situ TEM and ex situ x-ray diffraction techniques, the authors explain the large capacity of the anode through a dual mechanism of intercalation of Na ions along the x axis of the phosphorene layers followed by the formation of a Na3P alloy.  The presence of graphene layers in the hybrid material works as a mech. backbone and an elec. highway, ensuring that a suitable elastic buffer space accommodates the anisotropic expansion of phosphorene layers along the y and z axial directions for stable cycling operation.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref21" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.5b00376"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gao, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liou, S.-C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">9</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">3254</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">3264</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A highly ordered nanostructured carbon-sulphur cathode for lithium-sulphur batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ji, Xiulei; Lee, Kyu Tae; Nazar, Linda F.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2009</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">500-506</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The Li-S batteries have been studied for over 2 decades, as it offers the possibility of high gravimetric capacities and theor. energy densities ranging up to a factor of 5 beyond conventional Li-ion systems.  The feasibility to approach such capacities by creating highly ordered interwoven composites was studied.  The conductive mesoporous C framework constrains S nanofiller growth within its channels and generates essential elec. contact to the insulating S.  The structure provides access to Li+ ingress/egress for reactivity with the S.  It is possible that the kinetic inhibition to diffusion within the framework and the sorption properties of the C aid in trapping the polysulfides formed during redox.  Polymer modification of the C surface further provides a chem. gradient that retards diffusion of these large anions out of the electrode, thus facilitating more complete reaction.  Reversible capacities up to 1320 mA-h/g are attained.  The assembly process is simple and broadly applicable, conceptually providing new opportunities for materials scientists for tailored design that can be extended to many different electrode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref35" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201303147"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, C.                 10.1002/anie.201303147</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DYang%252C%2BC.%2BP.%253B%2BXin%252C%2BS.%253B%2BYin%252C%2BY.%2BX.%253B%2BYe%252C%2BH.%253B%2BZhang%252C%2BJ.%253B%2BGuo%252C%2BY.%2BG.Angew.%2BChem.%252C%2BInt.%2BEd.%2B2013%252C%2B52%252C%2B8363%25E2%2580%25938367&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.5b03903&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fanie.201303147&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A mesoporous Li4Ti5O12/C nanocomposite is synthesized by a nanocasting technique using the porous carbon material CMK-3 as a hard template.  Modified CMK-3 template is impregnated with Li4Ti5O12 precursor, followed by heat treatment at 750 °C for 6 h under N2.  Li4Ti5O12 nanocrystals of up to several tens of nanometers are successfully synthesized in micrometer-sized porous carbon foam to form a highly conductive network, as confirmed by field emission SEM, transmission electron microscopy, X-ray diffraction, Raman spectroscopy, and nitrogen sorption isotherms.  The composite is then evaluated as an anode material for lithium ion batteries.  It exhibits greatly improved electrochem. performance compared with bulk Li4Ti5O12, and shows an excellent rate capability (73.4 mA h g-1 at 80 C) with significantly enhanced cycling performance (only 5.6% capacity loss after 1000 cycles at a high rate of 20 C).  The greatly enhanced lithium storage properties of the mesoporous Li4Ti5O12/C nanocomposite may be attributed to the interpenetrating conductive carbon network, ordered mesoporous structure, and the small Li4Ti5O12 nanocrystallites that increase the ionic and electronic conduction throughout the electrode.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref37" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201402813"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Du, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shen, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Extremely high-rate capacity and stable cycling of a highly ordered nanostructured carbon-FeF2 battery cathode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Song, Huawei; Cui, Hao; Wang, Chengxin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">44</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">22377-22384</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">FeF2, as a promising cathode material for Li-ion batteries, has a high specific capacity of 571 mA h g-1, and a lot of research was focused on overcoming its poor cycling stability assocd. with low electron conduction and large vol. effect, mostly through nanostructured material design.  However, FeF2 nano-design itself is a challenge.  Herein, the authors report the incorporation of an ordered mesoporous C (CMK-3) into FeF2-based cathodes.  The FeF2 nanoparticles inside the conducting CMK-3 by topochem. conversion from an Fe oxide precursor to Fe fluoride hydrate in situ, form a well-connected 3 dimensional network structure.  Such a hierarchical framework combines multiple advantageous features, including a continuous elec. conductive network and porous space for the vol. expansion of the FeF2 particles.  With this cathode, the authors demonstrate a cycle life of 1000 cycles with little capacity decay (&lt;0.3‰ per cycle).  The FeF2@CMK-3 electrode shows stable cycling and an extremely high-rate capacity, owing to the special porous structure and the nano-sized particles.  In the potential range of 1.5-4.5 V, discharge capacities of 500, 400 and 320 mA h g-1 can be delivered at the high rates of 500, 2000 and 4000 mA g-1 after 100 cycles, resp., which is the highest level for FeF2 so far.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref44" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA04732J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pang, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nie, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shen, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, C.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Mater. Chem. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">2</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">20659</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">20666</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C4TA04732J</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DPang%252C%2BG.%253B%2BNie%252C%2BP.%253B%2BYuan%252C%2BC.%253B%2BShen%252C%2BL.%253B%2BZhang%252C%2BX.%253B%2BLi%252C%2BH.%253B%2BZhang%252C%2BC.J.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%2B2014%252C%2B2%252C%2B20659%25E2%2580%259320666&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.5b03903&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC4TA04732J&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mesoporous NaTi2(PO4)3/CMK-3 nanohybrid as anode for long-life Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pang, Gang; Nie, Ping; Yuan, Changzhou; Shen, Laifa; Zhang, Xiaogang; Li, Hongsen; Zhang, Cunliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">48</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20659-20666</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, a solvothermal strategy combined with following calcination was developed to synthesize a mesoporous NaTi2(PO4)3/CMK-3 nanohybrid as a high-performance anode for next-generation Na-ion batteries.  Physicochem. characterizations demonstrated that NASICON-type structured NaTi2(PO4)3 nanoparticles with high crystallinity were homogeneously embedded in the mesoporous CMK-3 matrix.  The mesoporous NaTi2(PO4)3/C nanohybrid as the anode for Na-ion batteries exhibited excellent electrochem. performance with high charge-discharge capability, good rate performance and long cycle life in nonaq. electrolytes.  The nanohybrid electrode delivered large specific capacities of 101, 76, 58, 39 mA-h/g at 0.2C, 0.5C, 1.0C and 2.0C, resp., and the specific capacity was still as high as 62.9 mA-h/g even after 1000 cycles at 0.5C.  Compared to the pure NaTi2(PO4)3 electrode, the mesoporous NaTi2(PO4)3/C hybrid anode with unique "meso-nano" architecture exhibited better Na-storage ability and indicated its promising application for rechargeable Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref45" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1002/asia.201300279"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, X. L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, Y. G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wan, L. J.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem. - Asian J.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1948</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1958</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/asia.201300279</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DWu%252C%2BX.%2BL.%253B%2BGuo%252C%2BY.%2BG.%253B%2BWan%252C%2BL.%2BJ.Chem.%2B-%2BAsian%2BJ.%2B2013%252C%2B8%252C%2B1948%25E2%2580%25931958&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.5b03903&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fasia.201300279&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational design materials based on group IVA elements (Si, Ge, and Sn) for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xing-Long; Guo, Yu-Guo; Wan, Li-Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - An Asian Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1948-1958</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CAAJBI</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1861-4728</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) represent the state-of-the-art technol. in rechargeable energy-storage devices and they currently occupy the prime position in the marketplace for powering an increasingly diverse range of applications.  However, the fast development of these applications has led to increasing demands being placed on advanced LIBs in terms of higher energy/power densities and longer life cycles.  For LIBs to meet these requirements, researchers have focused on active electrode materials, owing to their crucial roles in the electrochem. performance of batteries.  For anode materials, compds. based on Group IVA (Si, Ge, and Sn) elements represent one of the directions in the development of high-capacity anodes.  Although these compds. have many significant advantages when used as anode materials for LIBs, there are still some crit. problems to be solved before they can meet the high requirements for practical applications.  In this Focus Review, we summarize a series of rational designs for Group IVA-based anode materials, in terms of their chem. compns. and structures, that could address these problems, i.e., huge vol. variations during cycling, unstable surfaces/interfaces, and invalidation of transport pathways for electrons upon cycling.  These designs should at least include one of the following structural benefits: 1) Contain a sufficient no. of voids to accommodate the vol. variations during cycling; 2) adopt a "plum-pudding"-like structure to limit the vol. variations during cycling; 3) facilitate an efficient and permanent transport pathway for electrons and lithium ions; or 4) show stable surfaces/interfaces to stabilize the in situ formed SEI layers.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref46" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1039/c2nr31822a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wan, L.-J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, Y.-G.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">4</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">5868</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">5871</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c2nr31822a</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DZhou%252C%2BX.%253B%2BWan%252C%2BL.-J.%253B%2BGuo%252C%2BY.-G.Nanoscale%2B2012%252C%2B4%252C%2B5868%25E2%2580%25935871&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.5b03903&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc2nr31822a&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

C.; Thornton, K.; Van der Ven, A.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Much of current research in electrochem. energy storage is devoted to new electrode chemistries and reaction mechanisms that promise substantial increases in energy d.  Unfortunately, most high capacity electrodes exhibit an unacceptably large hysteresis in their voltage profile.  Using a first-principles multi-scale approach to examine particle level dynamics, we identify intrinsic thermodn. and kinetic properties that are responsible for the large hysteresis exhibited by many high capacity electrodes.  Our anal. shows that the hysteresis in the voltage profile of high capacity electrodes that rely on displacement reactions arises from a difference in reaction paths between charge and discharge.  We demonstrate that different reaction paths are followed (i) when there is a large mismatch in ionic mobilities between the electrochem. active species (e.g. Li) and displaced ionic species and (ii) when there is a lack of a thermodn. driving force to redistribute displaced ions upon charging of the electrode.  These insights motivate the formulation of design metrics for displacement reactions in terms of fundamental properties detd. by the chem. and crystallog. of the electrode material, properties that are now readily accessible with first-principles computation.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1039/c1ee01598b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Etacheri, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Marom, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Elazari, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Salitra, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Aurbach, D.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ. Li-ion battery technol. has become very important in recent years as these batteries show great promise as power sources that can lead us to the elec. vehicle (EV) revolution.  The development of new materials for Li-ion batteries is the focus of research in prominent groups in the field of materials science throughout the world.  Li-ion batteries can be considered to be the most impressive success story of modern electrochem. in the last two decades.  They power most of today's portable devices, and seem to overcome the psychol. barriers against the use of such high energy d. devices on a larger scale for more demanding applications, such as EV.  Since this field is advancing rapidly and attracting an increasing no. of researchers, it is important to provide current and timely updates of this constantly changing technol.  In this review, we describe the key aspects of Li-ion batteries: the basic science behind their operation, the most relevant components, anodes, cathodes, electrolyte solns., as well as important future directions for R&amp;D of advanced Li-ion batteries for demanding use, such as EV and load-leveling applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1039/c2ee02781j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Palomares, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Serras, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Villaluenga, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hueso, K.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.cossms.2012.04.002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ellis, B.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Owing to almost unmatched volumetric energy d., Li-ion batteries have dominated the portable electronics industry and solid state electrochem. literature for the past 20 years.  Not only will that continue, but they are also now powering plug-in hybrid elec. vehicles and elec. vehicles.  In light of possible concerns over rising lithium costs in the future, Na and Na-ion batteries have re-emerged as candidates for medium and large-scale stationary energy storage, esp. as a result of heightened interest in renewable energy sources that provide intermittent power which needs to be load-levelled.  The sodium-ion battery field presents many solid state materials design challenges, and rising to that call in the past couple of years, several reports of new sodium-ion technologies and electrode materials have surfaced.  These range from high-temp. air electrodes to new layered oxides, polyanion-based materials, carbons and other insertion materials for sodium-ion batteries, many of which hold promise for future sodium-based energy storage applications.  In this article, the challenges of current high-temp. sodium technologies including Na-S and Na-NiCl2 and new molten sodium technol., Na-O2 are summarized.  Recent advancements in pos. and neg. electrode materials suitable for Na-ion and hybrid Na/Li-ion cells are reviewed, along with the prospects for future developments.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201200691"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Slater, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Si-based Li-ion battery anodes have recently received great attention, as they offer specific capacity an order of magnitude beyond that of conventional graphite.  The applications of this transformative technol. require synthesis routes capable of producing safe and easy-to-handle anode particles with low vol. changes and stable performance during battery operation.  Herein, we report a large-scale hierarchical bottom-up assembly route for the formation of Si on the nanoscale-contg. rigid and robust spheres with irregular channels for rapid access of Li ions into the particle bulk.  Large Si vol. changes on Li insertion and extn. are accommodated by the particle's internal porosity.  Reversible capacities over five times higher than that of the state-of-the-art anodes and stable performance are attained.  The synthesis process is simple, low-cost, safe and broadly applicable, providing new avenues for the rational engineering of electrode materials with enhanced cond. and power.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1039/c3ee41031e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Palomares, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Casas-Cabanas, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Castillo-Martínez, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, M.                         rightTab-cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrode materials for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries: potential alternatives to current lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Sung-Wook; Seo, Dong-Hwa; Ma, Xiaohua; Ceder, Gerbrand; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium (Li)-ion batteries (LIB) have governed the current worldwide rechargeable battery market due to their outstanding energy and power capability.  In particular, the LIB's role in enabling elec. vehicles (EVs) has been highlighted to replace the current oil-driven vehicles in order to reduce the usage of oil resources and generation of CO2 gases.  Unlike Li, sodium is one of the more abundant elements on Earth and exhibits similar chem. properties to Li, indicating that Na chem. could be applied to a similar battery system.  In the 1970s-80s, both Na-ion and Li-ion electrodes were investigated, but the higher energy d. of Li-ion cells made them more applicable to small, portable electronic devices, and research efforts for rechargeable batteries have been mainly concd. on LIB since then.  Recently, research interest in Na-ion batteries (NIB) has been resurrected, driven by new applications with requirements different from those in portable electronics, and to address the concern on Li abundance.  In this article, both neg. and pos. electrode materials in NIB are briefly reviewed.  While the voltage is generally lower and the vol. change upon Na removal or insertion is larger for Na-intercalation electrodes, compared to their Li equiv., the power capability can vary depending on the crystal structures.  It is concluded that cost-effective NIB can partially replace LIB, but requires further investigation and improvement.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1039/C3NR05022J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zeng, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Y.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">6</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">693</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">698</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">With the expected theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1, P is considered to be the highest capacity anode material for Na-ion batteries and one of the most attractive anode materials for Li-ion systems.  This work presents a comprehensive study of P-C nanocomposite anodes for both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  The composite electrodes are able to display high initial capacities of ∼1700 and 1300 mA h g-1 in Li and Na half-cells, resp., when the cells are tested within a larger potential windows of 2.0-0.01 V vs. Li/Li+ and Na/Na+.  The level of demonstrated capacity is underpinned by the storage mechanism, based on the transformation of P to Li3P phase for Li cells and an incomplete transformation to Na3P phase for Na cells.  The capacity deteriorates upon cycling, which is shown to originate from disintegration of electrodes and their delamination from current collectors by post-cycling ex situ electron microscopy.  Stable cyclic performance at the level of ∼700 and ∼350-400 mA h g-1 can be achieved if the potential windows are restricted to 2.0-0.67 V vs. Li/Li+ for Li and 2-0.33 vs. Na/Na+ for Na half-cells.  The results are critically discussed in light of literature reports.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref16" class="rightTabRefNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit16" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2014.07.026"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Y.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Carbon</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">78</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">455</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">462</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

At fixed pressure, a time dependent variation of resistance occurred due to relaxation of the glass structure.  Temp. dependence of the resistance at const. pressure suggests that the variable-range hopping becomes the dominant conduction mechanism as pressure is increased; an increase in the no. of defect sites is responsible for the decrease in resistance.  A comparison is made with other materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1002/adma.200602592"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, C.                         rightTab-cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A phosphorene-graphene hybrid material as a high-capacity anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Jie; Lee, Hyun-Wook; Pasta, Mauro; Yuan, Hongtao; Zheng, Guangyuan; Sun, Yongming; Li, Yuzhang; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Nanotechnology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">980-985</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NNAABX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1748-3387</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have recently attracted significant attention as an alternative to Li-ion batteries because Na sources do not present the geopolitical issues that Li sources might.  Although recent reports on cathode materials for Na-ion batteries demonstrated performances comparable to their Li-ion counterparts, the major scientific challenge for a competitive Na-ion battery technol. is to develop viable anode materials.  A hybrid material made out of a few phosphorene layers sandwiched between graphene layers shows a specific capacity of 2 440 mA h g-1 (calcd. using the mass of P only) at a c.d. of 0.05 A g-1 and an 83% capacity retention after 100 cycles while operating between 0 and 1.5 V.  Using in situ TEM and ex situ x-ray diffraction techniques, the authors explain the large capacity of the anode through a dual mechanism of intercalation of Na ions along the x axis of the phosphorene layers followed by the formation of a Na3P alloy.  The presence of graphene layers in the hybrid material works as a mech. backbone and an elec. highway, ensuring that a suitable elastic buffer space accommodates the anisotropic expansion of phosphorene layers along the y and z axial directions for stable cycling operation.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref21" class="rightTabRefNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit21" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.5b00376"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gao, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liou, S.-C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">9</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">3254</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">3264</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nazar, L. F.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.                 10.1038/nmat2460</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A highly ordered nanostructured carbon-sulphur cathode for lithium-sulphur batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ji, Xiulei; Lee, Kyu Tae; Nazar, Linda F.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2009</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">500-506</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The Li-S batteries have been studied for over 2 decades, as it offers the possibility of high gravimetric capacities and theor. energy densities ranging up to a factor of 5 beyond conventional Li-ion systems.  The feasibility to approach such capacities by creating highly ordered interwoven composites was studied.  The conductive mesoporous C framework constrains S nanofiller growth within its channels and generates essential elec. contact to the insulating S.  The structure provides access to Li+ ingress/egress for reactivity with the S.  It is possible that the kinetic inhibition to diffusion within the framework and the sorption properties of the C aid in trapping the polysulfides formed during redox.  Polymer modification of the C surface further provides a chem. gradient that retards diffusion of these large anions out of the electrode, thus facilitating more complete reaction.  Reversible capacities up to 1320 mA-h/g are attained.  The assembly process is simple and broadly applicable, conceptually providing new opportunities for materials scientists for tailored design that can be extended to many different electrode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref35" class="rightTabRefNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit35" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201303147"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, C.                         rightTab-cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Li4Ti5O12 nanoparticles embedded in a mesoporous carbon matrix as a superior anode material for high rate lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shen, Laifa; Zhang, Xiaogang; Uchaker, Evan; Yuan, Changzhou; Cao, Guozhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A mesoporous Li4Ti5O12/C nanocomposite is synthesized by a nanocasting technique using the porous carbon material CMK-3 as a hard template.  Modified CMK-3 template is impregnated with Li4Ti5O12 precursor, followed by heat treatment at 750 °C for 6 h under N2.  Li4Ti5O12 nanocrystals of up to several tens of nanometers are successfully synthesized in micrometer-sized porous carbon foam to form a highly conductive network, as confirmed by field emission SEM, transmission electron microscopy, X-ray diffraction, Raman spectroscopy, and nitrogen sorption isotherms. The greatly enhanced lithium storage properties of the mesoporous Li4Ti5O12/C nanocomposite may be attributed to the interpenetrating conductive carbon network, ordered mesoporous structure, and the small Li4Ti5O12 nanocrystallites that increase the ionic and electronic conduction throughout the electrode.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref37" class="rightTabRefNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit37" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201402813"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Du, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shen, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">FeF2, as a promising cathode material for Li-ion batteries, has a high specific capacity of 571 mA h g-1, and a lot of research was focused on overcoming its poor cycling stability assocd. with low electron conduction and large vol. effect, mostly through nanostructured material design.  However, FeF2 nano-design itself is a challenge.  Herein, the authors report the incorporation of an ordered mesoporous C (CMK-3) into FeF2-based cathodes.  The FeF2 nanoparticles inside the conducting CMK-3 by topochem. conversion from an Fe oxide precursor to Fe fluoride hydrate in situ, form a well-connected 3 dimensional network structure.  Such a hierarchical framework combines multiple advantageous features, including a continuous elec. conductive network and porous space for the vol. expansion of the FeF2 particles.  With this cathode, the authors demonstrate a cycle life of 1000 cycles with little capacity decay (&lt;0.3‰ per cycle).  The FeF2@CMK-3 electrode shows stable cycling and an extremely high-rate capacity, owing to the special porous structure and the nano-sized particles.  In the potential range of 1.5-4.5 V, discharge capacities of 500, 400 and 320 mA h g-1 can be delivered at the high rates of 500, 2000 and 4000 mA g-1 after 100 cycles, resp., which is the highest level for FeF2 so far.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref44" class="rightTabRefNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit44" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA04732J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pang, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nie, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shen, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, C.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, a solvothermal strategy combined with following calcination was developed to synthesize a mesoporous NaTi2(PO4)3/CMK-3 nanohybrid as a high-performance anode for next-generation Na-ion batteries.  Physicochem. characterizations demonstrated that NASICON-type structured NaTi2(PO4)3 nanoparticles with high crystallinity were homogeneously embedded in the mesoporous CMK-3 matrix.  The mesoporous NaTi2(PO4)3/C nanohybrid as the anode for Na-ion batteries exhibited excellent electrochem. performance with high charge-discharge capability, good rate performance and long cycle life in nonaq. electrolytes. Compared to the pure NaTi2(PO4)3 electrode, the mesoporous NaTi2(PO4)3/C hybrid anode with unique "meso-nano" architecture exhibited better Na-storage ability and indicated its promising application for rechargeable Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref45" class="rightTabRefNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit45" data-doi="10.1002/asia.201300279"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, X.                         rightTab-cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational design materials based on group IVA elements (Si, Ge, and Sn) for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xing-Long; Guo, Yu-Guo; Wan, Li-Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - An Asian Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1948-1958</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CAAJBI</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1861-4728</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) represent the state-of-the-art technol. in rechargeable energy-storage devices and they currently occupy the prime position in the marketplace for powering an increasingly diverse range of applications.  However, the fast development of these applications has led to increasing demands being placed on advanced LIBs in terms of higher energy/power densities and longer life cycles.  For LIBs to meet these requirements, researchers have focused on active electrode materials, owing to their crucial roles in the electrochem. performance of batteries.  For anode materials, compds. based on Group IVA (Si, Ge, and Sn) elements represent one of the directions in the development of high-capacity anodes.  Although these compds. have many significant advantages when used as anode materials for LIBs, there are still some crit. problems to be solved before they can meet the high requirements for practical applications.  In this Focus Review, we summarize a series of rational designs for Group IVA-based anode materials, in terms of their chem. compns. and structures, that could address these problems, i.e., huge vol. variations during cycling, unstable surfaces/interfaces, and invalidation of transport pathways for electrons upon cycling.  These designs should at least include one of the following structural benefits: 1) Contain a sufficient no. of voids to accommodate the vol. variations during cycling; 2) adopt a "plum-pudding"-like structure to limit the vol. variations during cycling; 3) facilitate an efficient and permanent transport pathway for electrons and lithium ions; or 4) show stable surfaces/interfaces to stabilize the in situ formed SEI layers.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref46" class="rightTabRefNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit46" data-doi="10.1039/c2nr31822a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wan, L.-J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, Y.-G.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">4</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">5868</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">5871</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c2nr31822a</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref47" class="rightTabRefNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit47" data-doi="10.1021/nn501945f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Song, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.-C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">van Aken, P. A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Maier, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Y.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">7051</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">7059</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nn501945f</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-2"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i1">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acs.nanolett.5b03903" class="ext-link">10.1021/acs.nanolett.5b03903</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Additional information and figures: Preparation and characterization methods, electrochemical characterization parameters, N<sub>2</sub> sorption/desorption result, EDX elemental mapping images, TGA results, electrochemical performance, comparison of electrochemical performance, SEM, TEM and HRTEM images, Nyquist plots (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.5b03903/suppl_file/nl5b03903_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.5b03903/suppl_file/nl5b03903_si_001.pdf">nl5b03903_si_001.pdf (2.43 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

        <script nonce="93187f8fde95075b-SJC">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="93187f8fde95075b-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

      var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage =
          "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

      function init() {
        setTimeout(function () {
          var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
          if (cookieExist) {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
            return false;
          } else {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
            gdprMessage();
          }
          //Events
          $("#closebtn").on("click", hideForm);

          //Handle submit
          $("#gdpr-message-btn").on("click", function (event) {
            handleClick();
          });

          // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
          // $(document).click(function(event) {
          // 	event.stopPropagation();
          //   console.log(event.target);
          //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
          //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();

            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            hideForm();
          });

      //Show the message
      function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();
      }

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
      }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;
          $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
      }

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

    $(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
  </script>

        <script nonce="93187f8fde95075b-SJC">
var currentJournal = "Nano Letters";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>

$(document).ready(function(){
    var cookie = "";
    var uri = "/doi/full/10.1021/html_original_uri?id=123";
    console.log("ACSPubs2 start");
    $.getJSON('https://extreme-ip-lookup.com/json/', function(data, status) {
            if ( status == 'success' ) {
                $.each(data, function(i, field){
                    cookie=cookie.concat(i+' = '+field+" - ");
                });
                
            } else {
                    cookie=status;
            }

            cookie1 = cookie;
            cookie = cookie1 + "; path=/; domain=.acs.org";
            //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
            $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.
            //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
            console.log("ACSPubs2 success");
    })
    .fail(function(xx, status, err){
        cookie="error: 127.0.0.1";
        //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
        $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.

    });
